GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
f(P)=0.5980421691\,(1-\tfrac{P}{32.9394024023})P+0.5980421691\,(1-e^{-0.07682777496P})P
\]
So
- it is **independent of \(t\)**,
- it equals \(aP-a\frac{P^2}{32.9394}+aP-aP e^{-kP}\) with \(a=0.5980,\ k=0.0768278\),
- crucially it contains the non-algebraic term **\(P e^{-kP}\)** (an exponential in \(P\), multiplied by \(P\)), and also polynomial terms in \(P\).

To match GT exactly for all \(P\ge 0, t\ge 0\), a candidate must be able to produce a term of the form \(P e^{-kP}\) (with \(k\neq 0\)) and must not introduce any unavoidable \(t\)-dependence.

---

### 1
\(P^2(\cdot)+P(\cdot)+P\frac{c3}{P+c4}+c5 e^{c6 t}\). No exponential in \(P\); has possible \(t\)-term unless killed. Even with \(c5=0\), cannot create \(P e^{-kP}\). **No.**

### 2
\(P^2 c0 + Pc1 + P c2\log(Pc3+1)+c4\). Has \(\log\), no \(e^{-kP}\). **No.**

### 6

### 7

You could try \(c2=0\) to remove denominator, but then you get \(P\exp(Pc4)\) and/or \(P^2\exp(Pc4)\); you cannot simultaneously eliminate the \(P^2\exp(Pc4)\) part while keeping \(P\exp(Pc4)\) unless you set its coefficient to 0, but then you lose the needed exponential term. Also Max(0,P+c1) cannot equal \(P\) for all \(P\ge0\) unless \(c1=0\), but then it becomes \(P\) and introduces \(P^2\) scaling in those terms. Overall cannot reproduce exactly \(P e^{-kP}\) plus the specific polynomial part without extra structures. **No.**

### 19
Has \(P c2 e^{P c3}\) which can produce \(P e^{-kP}\) by setting \(c3=-k\). But the rest is \(P*c0*Max(0,P+c1)+P*c4+P^{c5}c6+c7\).  
To match GT’s polynomial part, we need a **\(P^2\)** term with a specific coefficient and a **\(P\)** term with a specific coefficient, and no Max kink. If we set \(c1=0\), then \(P*c0*Max(0,P)=c0 P^2\) (good for a \(P^2\) term). We can set \(c0\) to match \(-a/32.9394\). We can set \(c4\) to match the linear \(P\) coefficient. We can set \(c5\) so that \(P^{c5}c6\) vanishes (take \(c6=0\)). Set \(c7=0\).  
However, GT’s exponential term is **\(-a P e^{-kP}\)** plus also **a +aP term** already accounted in linear coefficient. Candidate’s exponential term is \(+P c2 e^{Pc3}\). We can set \(c2=-a\) and \(c3=-k\) to match \(-a P e^{-kP}\).  
So far this looks promising, but check the remaining polynomial part: GT polynomial part is
\[
aP - a\frac{P^2}{32.9394} + aP
= 2aP - a\frac{P^2}{32.9394}.
\]
Candidate polynomial part (after choices) is \(c0 P^2 + c4 P\). That can match by setting \(c0=-a/32.9394\) and \(c4=2a\). This is feasible. Also Max term with \(c1=0\) is smooth for \(P\ge0\) (equals \(P\)).  
Thus candidate 19 **can** exactly represent GT by parameter choice:
- \(c1=0\)
- \(c0=-a/32.9394024023\)
- \(c4=2a\)
- \(c2=-a\)
- \(c3=-k\)
- \(c6=0\) (any \(c5\))
- \(c7=0\)

So **Yes, 19 matches**.
